Local News

Min Pirates Rob Xinming Steamer 114

More than 30 pirates disguised as steerage passengers

Forcing the ship to Red Sea Bay as it approached Fuzhou Port

Holding the radio operator's room at gunpoint

Robbing goods and kidnapping passengers and four crew members

There are the most pirates along the Nanyang route, and cases of robbing merchant ships often occur. The Nanhua steamers of British merchants Taikoo and Jardine Matheson in Shanghai have already implemented the addition of armed guards stationed on the ships for protection. The China Merchants Bureau is also planning to increase the number of guards stationed on Nanyang steamers, but it has not yet been implemented. The Xinming steamer was robbed again in the Min Sea, goods were robbed, and passengers were kidnapped, resulting in huge losses. The details of the incident are reported as follows:

The reason for the robbery: The Xinming steamer of the China Merchants Bureau was originally a North China special run, but this time, due to the freezing of North China, it was reassigned to the Fuzhou run. The ship departed from Shanghai on the 9th with many passengers and goods. When the ship departed from Shanghai, more than 30 pirates disguised as steerage passengers boarded the ship to Fujian. Although they were inspected at the time, no weapons were found. There was no movement when the ship left Wusong. On the afternoon of the 10th, the Xinming steamer had arrived at the outer port of Fuzhou. The captain was about to sail into the port of Min when, unexpectedly, these more than 30 pirates disguised as passengers swarmed out of the lower deck, each holding pistols and boxes, and wearing identifying marks on their bodies. The bandits divided into several groups, one group rushing to the captain's room, the radio room, and the driver's room, and the other group guarding all the crew members. Then they proceeded to rob.

Forcing the ship to Red Sea Bay: The bandits detained all the crew members in one place and ordered the helmsman not to enter Fuzhou Port but to sail to Red Sea Bay. Red Sea Bay is the junction of Shantou, Xiamen, Hong Kong, and Guangzhou, and pirates had already sent pirate ships to wait there. At this time, the entire ship was controlled by bandits, and the driver dared not resist, so he had to sail to Red Sea Bay. There was a radio on board, and the radio operator tried to send a distress signal during the robbery but was beaten and stopped by the bandits. Therefore, the robbery went smoothly all the way, and there were several warships nearby, but the crew members could not ask for help.

Searching and robbing goods: The search and robbery began in the middle of the night on the 10th, first robbing the money on the ship, and then searching the passengers' belongings. When they arrived at Red Sea Bay, it was already the morning of the 11th. After the money and goods were robbed, the cargo holds were also opened. The valuable goods loaded on the ship, such as textiles, wool, cotton yarn, and imported miscellaneous goods, were all robbed from the upper decks and placed on the deck. When the ship arrived at its destination in Red Sea Bay, the pirate ships were already waiting there. The bandits placed the robbed items one by one on the lifeboats of the Xinming steamer, put them into the sea, and transferred them to the pirate ships. The bandits also went with them.

Passengers kidnapped: When the bandits left the ship, they still felt that the robbed money and goods were not enough, so they kidnapped passengers Chen and Zhong from the large dining room and two passengers from the officer's cabin together on a sampan and押into the pirate ship. The ship's inspector Jiang was also robbed along with them. It was said that each person had to pay 50,000 to 100,000 yuan to be redeemed. Wang Binghou, the director of the Fuzhou branch of the China Merchants Bureau, was also on board to Fuzhou. He temporarily pretended to be a low-level crew member and was spared from being kidnapped, which was also fortunate.

The captain wired the Shanghai Bureau: After the bandits left, the captain and others were released by the passengers and inspected the losses. They immediately sailed the ship to Xiamen and sent two telegrams to the Shanghai General Bureau, reporting that the Xinming steamer was robbed on the night of the 10th, sailed to Red Sea Bay, and then the bandits left the ship, robbing two passengers surnamed Chen and Zhong from the special-class room, as well as two officer's cabin passengers whose names are unknown, and an inspector from the business department. A lifeboat was also robbed. The rest of the crew members on the ship were all safe. Now the ship's food supply is cut off. They are going to Xiamen first and ask the General Bureau to telegraph the Xiamen branch to provide food. At a minimum, the ship needs enough coal and food to go to Fuzhou so that it can be replenished after arriving in Fujian.

The General Bureau's thorough investigation: Yesterday afternoon, the Shanghai Bureau received the second telegram, knowing that the Xinming had arrived in Xiamen, and the General Administration immediately telegraphed the Fuzhou and Xiamen branches to fully supply the Xinming with food and fuel. At the same time, the two branches and the captain of the Xinming were ordered to thoroughly investigate the cause of the incident and the amount of damage. A telegram was also sent to the Xiamen Navy, requesting them to send warships to pursue the pirates as soon as possible to maintain commercial navigation. After the local newspapers received this shocking report yesterday, many passengers went to the bureau to inquire. Although there was no detailed report on the amount of loss, it was at least between 200,000 and 300,000 yuan.

Sino-German Aviation Corporation 115

Board of directors to be convened within the week to proceed with everything

Purchase of aircraft and recruitment of staff to begin immediately

Eurasia Aviation to conduct test flights in mid-February

Eurasia Aviation, which was planned by the former Beijing government, was finally organized last year when seven ministers of the Ministry of Communications and Schmidt, the representative of the German Lufthansa, signed a contract. The Ministry of Communications also sent Shuang Qing and Mo Yong to Europe to inspect telecommunications and aviation administration and to discuss the Eurasia Aviation issue. They have now returned home via Siberia and arrived in Beijing on the 7th. They met with Minister Wang to report everything and came to Shanghai from Beijing the day before yesterday for a short rest. A reporter from the Xinsheng News Agency met Mr. Mo at a certain place yesterday and talked in detail about Eurasia Aviation. The details are as follows:

Returning from inspection: I (Mo himself) was assigned to go to Europe with Mr. Shuang Qing to inspect telecommunications and aviation administration. I attended the International Radio Conference in Belgium at the end of September last year. In addition, I went abroad for eight months to discuss Eurasia Aviation. Excluding the two months for traveling, I spent four months inspecting telecommunications and aviation administration and attending the Radio Conference, and the rest of the time in Germany discussing Eurasia Aviation. This time, I returned home via Siberia and arrived in Beijing on the 7th. I came to Shanghai on the 9th for a short rest.

Situation in Europe: The economic situation in Europe has been quite alarming recently, especially with the most unemployment in Germany. Since Germany's defeat in the war, it has had to pay reparations of 250 million marks every year, which will increase every year until it is paid off in 1960. The German government has no definite income to offset this. Commerce is controlled by Jews. What the Germans rely on is only the development of machinery. The competition among countries is also very fierce, so factories with less capital have difficulty maintaining themselves. There are more than 3.5 million unemployed people. Next year, the railway income will be increased by 100 million by raising ticket prices, and the tax income will be 150 million. On average, people have to bear more than 20% of their income. The high cost of living can be imagined. This is my second trip to Europe, but I feel that the business of Europe has improved a lot compared to previous years. Even in Germany alone, the invention of machinery in aviation administration and telecommunications is amazing. We should catch up as soon as possible.

Eurasia Aviation: The original agreement for Eurasia Aviation stipulated three lines: one line going abroad from Xinjiang to Germany, one line going to Germany via Mongolia and Siberia, and one line going from Manzhouli. The Russian government has not yet fully agreed. However, this section of the route is handled by Germany. This is entirely a matter for the German Lufthansa and the Russian government, and our country does not need to interfere too much. There is a Soviet-German joint venture airline, Tai Luoluofu 脱航空 Company, between Moscow and Berlin. The Russian government has also established a national airline from Moscow to Irkutsk. If the Russian government cannot fully agree to the Sino-German Aviation Company's passage through Russia, then Sino-German mail transport between Manzhouli and Moscow may be handled by the Russian National Aviation Company, and the Moscow-Berlin section may be handled by the Soviet-German joint venture airline. Mr. Furansk, the manager of the Masha Company, plans to go to Russia in person to discuss this matter. If the negotiations go smoothly, it will only take three or four days to go from Beijing to Berlin.

Test flights are imminent: We have ordered four aircraft from Lufthansa in Germany. One aircraft can be shipped before February 10, and the remaining two aircraft can arrive within a month. We have also hired four pilots, one mechanic, eight technicians, and one person familiar with business, for a total of fourteen people, who will come to China in two batches. The first batch will arrive on February 1, and the second batch will arrive on March 1. All four aircraft have been carefully inspected and selected by Lufthansa and ordered from the German National Aviation Testing Institute, which has issued certificates. The pilots have also been selected and approved by the German Ministry of Transport, which has issued certificates. All four aircraft are land-based and can carry both passengers and cargo. Two aircraft are W33 models and two are Fr models. As soon as the aircraft arrive, test flights will be conducted in Manzhouli.

Calling a board meeting: Minister Wang believes that Eurasia Aviation needs to be opened urgently, and the Sino-German Aviation Corporation should be organized and established as soon as possible. It has been decided to convene a board meeting of the Chinese Aviation Corporation within this week and to urgently telegraph Schmidt, the representative of the German Lufthansa, who is staying in Beijing, to attend the meeting. It is said that the Chinese side of the board will be Wei Yiduan, Liu Shufan, Shuang Qing, Cong, etc., for a total of six people. On the German side, there will be a senior executive of the German Post Boat Company, Boer  Chen, Ban Gaofu, the most 洋行 businessman at the time, and Feng Xike, the senior executive of the Siemens 洋行. It is said that the board will discuss taking the Sino-German route through Harbin and Shenyang and has invited representatives from the Northeast to attend the meeting and consider opinions. It is said that one seat on the board will be held by Minister Wang and Vice Minister Wei Yifu, and the vice-chairmen will be the German representative Schmidt and the representative from the Northeast.

Organizing the company: The company is divided into three groups: operations, aviation, and finance. The heads of the operations and finance groups are Chinese and have been internally designated as Shuang Qing and Lin Tianlan. The deputy head of the aviation group has been internally designated as Mo Yong. The list of German heads and deputy heads has not yet been released and will be decided at this board meeting. The company will be temporarily established in Shanghai and will be moved to Beijing in the future. It is said that for the safety of passengers, mail, and staff, the company has decided to propose insurance at the board meeting. It is said that the company's new aircraft are all made by the Junkers factory and cost 40,000 to 50,000 marks each (one mark is approximately equal to one yuan in Chinese currency) and are extremely comfortable.

Business Conference to be Held Tomorrow on Two Railways 116

The venue is at the Jiande Savings Society

The Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Administrations, in order to develop business and facilitate passengers and merchants, have specially convened representatives from chambers of commerce and various industries along the two railways to hold a business conference. The preparatory procedures have now been completed, and the conference will be held from tomorrow. The news of the conference is recorded below.

The process of preparation: Since Liu Weizhi, the director of the Business Department of the Ministry of Railways, concurrently took charge of the affairs of the two railways, he realized that the two railways connect to the major trunk lines of Jinpu and Longhai to the north, reach Shanghai, the only seaport for international trade, to the east, and adjoin the provinces of Min and Anhui to the southwest. Moreover, the areas they pass through are densely populated and rich in products. According to their geographical situation, if the freight business is reorganized, there will be extraordinary progress. He had the intention of convening a business conference, but due to the outbreak of military affairs, various industries were suspended, and the railways were also busy with military transportation, so he had no time for this, and the matter was put on hold. After the end of the military affairs last winter, merchants eagerly hoped for the improvement of transportation, and the railway bureau also urgently needed to reorganize railway affairs. Therefore, it was felt that the business conference was of great importance to both the railway bureau and the merchants and could not be convened sooner. Therefore, it was decided to convene this conference to discuss and obtain results, which could be used as a standard for the development of transportation on the railway or submitted to the Ministry of Railways for approval and implementation. After this matter was decided, the director sent Zheng Baozhao, the director of the car affairs department of the two railways, to organize a preparatory committee with the director of the general affairs department to prepare everything. It was stipulated that all matters such as proposals and the hiring of representatives should be handled by the car affairs department, and all matters such as reception and general affairs should be handled by the general affairs department. It is said that since Zheng Baozhao, the director of the car affairs department, took on this matter, in addition to supervising the section chiefs and section chiefs to prepare proposals for discussion at the conference, he also sent letters to hire representatives from various industries and transportation experts to attend. By the end of last year, all the procedures had been completed. It was originally scheduled to be held on the 5th of this month, but due to requests from representatives from various foreign ports for postponement, it was changed to tomorrow.

Tomorrow's conference: The railway bureau estimates that the number of attendees at this conference will be more than 200. The railway bureau does not have a suitable venue inside, so it has specially borrowed the Jiande Savings Society on Fusheng Road. A special commissioner has been assigned to start arranging the venue, which is scheduled to be held at 9:00 AM tomorrow.

Representatives who have registered: It is said that the railway bureau has hired about 50 representatives from various cities and counties outside Shanghai, about 80 representatives from various industries and institutions in Shanghai, and about 10 transportation experts, for a total of about 140 people. Yesterday, dozens of representatives from outside Shanghai had registered. It is expected that all the representatives who have been invited will be able to attend the meeting as scheduled tomorrow.

Hotel rentals: The railway bureau believes that the representatives from various foreign ports who are coming to Shanghai to attend the conference may not be familiar with the situation in Shanghai and will feel inconvenient in terms of accommodation. Therefore, it has specially rented the centrally located, air-clean, and hospitable Central Hotel for the representatives from various foreign ports to stay at will, in order to fulfill its reception duties.

Classification of proposals: According to Zheng Baozhao, the director of the car affairs department of the two railways, as of yesterday, a total of 183 proposals have been received. They have now been classified according to the nature of each proposal into three categories for discussion in three groups in the future, namely: (1) station affairs group, issues such as loading and unloading goods and requesting cars; (2) freight rate group, freight issues for various goods; (3) transportation group, vehicle distribution issues. Among the three categories, the station affairs group has the most proposals.

Dramatic Increase in Japanese Imports of Chinese Cotton Yarn 117

Due to the sharp decline in silver prices, our country's exports of cotton yarn to Japan have recently been increasing daily. According to reliable sources, Japanese merchants have ordered more than 4,000 bales of cotton yarn from China this month. This cotton yarn will soon be shipped for export. If the current market price remains unchanged, Japanese cotton cloth merchants will order a large quantity of cotton yarn. In the first half of last year, the number of Chinese yarn exports to Japan averaged about 100 bales per day. By autumn, due to limited production by Japanese textile factories and a sudden increase in the demand for cotton cloth, Chinese yarn exports to Japan showed a lively atmosphere. Exports in September totaled more than 250 bales, increased to 800 bales in October, and decreased again to [blank] bales in November. In early December, Japanese yarn factories in the three eastern provinces [Manchuria] ordered a large quantity of Chinese yarn. In recent years, the Chinese and Japanese textile industries in the three eastern provinces have made great progress in actual production.

Chinese Refuse to Buy Japanese Fish 118

Japanese Consul Invites Fish Merchants to Advise

Claims Japanese Fishing Boats Are Not Fishing in Chinese Waters

Social Affairs Bureau to Make Concrete Representation

The Japanese Daily News reports that 32 Japanese fishing boats are fishing in the coastal waters of Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces in our country. The fact that they are overstepping their authority and infringing upon our interests is obvious and has attracted the attention of all sectors of our country and government authorities. The fish merchants in the 16th Pier area of Nanshi in this port, driven by patriotism, unanimously refused to sell Japanese fish a few days ago. Japanese fish merchants were greatly alarmed because the fish caught by the 32 fishing boats that crossed the sea to fish are all sold in Shanghai, with monthly transactions exceeding 400,000 yuan. Moreover, due to the crowding of fishing boats in Dalian and other places in Japan, the price of fish has gradually fallen. If Shanghai refuses to sell Japanese fish, future development will be hopeless, and they will suffer an immediate blow. Therefore, three days ago, the Japanese Consul in Shanghai invited the managers of fish shops in the 16th Pier area to the consulate to advise them, saying that the 32 fishing boats were not fishing in the coastal waters of China, and that all the fish stalls that came to Shanghai to sell fish were caught in the ocean. He asked that they continue to sell fish as usual. The managers of the fish shops did not respond and left in silence. However, in fact, they still do not sell Japanese fish. The Social Affairs Bureau of this city believes that the Japanese fishing boats go to the sea to fish and sell fish in Shanghai, which competes with the market and is greatly detrimental to national sovereignty and the Chinese fish industry. It is said that there will be concrete representations, approximately: (1) convening a meeting of the Ice Fresh Fish Merchants Association of this port to discuss and resolutely refuse to sell Japanese fish; (2) the Ministry of Agriculture and Mines had previously formulated regulations stipulating that any domestic merchants who operate their own fishing boats to catch fish must first apply to the local government, report to the provincial government, and then report to the Ministry of Agriculture and Mines for registration and licensing before they can implement their operations. Although the Ministry of Agriculture and Mines has now been merged into the Ministry of Industry, the effect of the laws and regulations still exists. The Japanese fishing boats fish in the coastal waters of our country without obtaining the permission of our government and without the approval of the Ministry's order, which violates the laws and regulations of our government and goes against international conventions. Therefore, this incident should be raised by our government in serious negotiations. In addition, the Jiangsu Provincial Department of Agriculture and Mines, the Shanghai Social Affairs Bureau, and the Jiangsu Fisheries Experimentation Institute have jointly launched a fisheries improvement propaganda meeting to expand publicity on the improvement of the Chinese fish industry and the opposition to Japanese fishing boats fishing across the sea. It is expected to be held in the middle of next month.

New Swedish Envoy in Shanghai Awaiting Meeting with Foreign Minister 119

Stays for a Month Before Assuming New Post in Japan

Hattman, the newly appointed Swedish envoy to China and concurrently minister to China, recently arrived in Shanghai and is staying at the Astor House Hotel. He went to the Foreign Affairs Office to take over and requested to schedule a meeting with Foreign Minister Wang Zhengting. Because the Foreign Minister was about to go to Tianjin, he promised to meet in Shanghai in two weeks. Mr. Hattman has decided to wait in Shanghai and informed Liu Yunfang of the Diplomatic Office yesterday that he will stay for more than a month. After the takeover is completed, he will go to Japan to assume his new post.

Wang Jiazhen Went North Yesterday Morning 120

Goes Directly to Jilin Native Place to Visit Relatives

Scheduled to Return to Beijing in Early February

Wang Jiazhen, Vice Minister of Foreign Affairs, has requested leave to return to his hometown to visit his father who is ill. Yesterday morning at 10 o'clock, he took the Japanese ship Changchun Maru directly to Dalian, and then transferred to Shuangcheng, his native place in Jilin. His family members stayed in Shanghai and did not travel with him. Those who came to the Huangpu Wharf to see him off yesterday morning included Mrs. Wang and Liu Yunhang and several others. According to Wang, he plans to stay for about ten days and then go south to cancel his leave and take up his duties. It is expected that he will be able to return to Beijing in early February.

Details of Commander Xiong's Resignation 121

The resignation of Xiong Shihui as commander of the Fifth Division and garrison commander of Songhu has been reported in previous newspapers. Xiong has been stationed in Shanghai twice, for a total of three years. He seems to have made no notable achievements in protecting the local area, which is his duty. However, stationed in this place where Chinese and foreigners live in mixed residence and where the trails of bandits and communists can be found, and at a time when the country is facing many difficulties, the rear has remained safe during the three times the central government has used troops. Xiong has also put in a lot of effort. It is said that Xiong, with the end of military affairs and the completion of unification, is very willing to leave Songhu and unload this heavy responsibility. Before taking a plane to Jiangxi, he personally presented to Commander-in-Chief Chiang his resignation from all his posts, and guaranteed that Hu Zuyu would succeed him as division commander. The Commander-in-Chief, because the majority of the Fifth Division had been led by Deputy Division Commander Hu Zuyu to northern Jiangxi to suppress bandits, and Xiong had no time to take care of it, seemed to agree to Xiong's resignation as division commander. At that time, Chiang was going to Jiangxi and intended for Xiong to go with him to preside over the affairs of the headquarters. Unfortunately, Xiong fell and was injured, which greatly disappointed Chiang. During the New Year, Chiang came to Shanghai to see Xiong's illness, and Xiong again personally presented his resignation, which was comforted and retained. Xiong finally feared that it would hinder his duties, and sent another telegram to resign, and entrusted Secretary-General Shao to submit it on his behalf. Now, he is only allowed to resign from his position as division commander, which seems to be the predetermined arrangement. As for Xiong's appointment as Vice Minister of Military and Political Affairs, it is said that this was only discussed before Xiong went to Jiangxi. The telegram of Xiong's resignation and the Commander-in-Chief's reply are found below for supplementary publication: (1) Xiong's telegram: Nanjing Commander-in-Chief Chiang Junjian Jian, Confidential, I was injured in this plane crash and need time to recover. The positions I hold as commander of the Fifth Division and garrison commander of Songhu are all important. The vacant position has been suspended for a long time, and there are many fears of delaying matters. For this reason, I am sincerely requesting your seat to approve my resignation from all my posts, so that I can rest and recuperate. If my illness recovers soon, then my future body will be used to serve the country. I cannot express my exhaustion while lying in bed waiting for orders. Sincerely, Xiong Shihui Koutou, Yu Yin. (2) Chiang's telegram: Shanghai Commander Xiong Tianyi Brother Xun Jian, I have read your telegram, Songhu is a place where Chinese and foreigners live in mixed residence, and there are many communist spies. Relying on your vigilance and maintenance, I am deeply pleased. Now, although you are injured in a plane crash, you will soon recover. Hu Zuyu is approved to succeed as commander of the Fifth Division, so that he can be solely responsible for the task. As for the position of garrison commander of Songhu, I still request you to assume it, so that you can maintain stability and recuperate with peace of mind. In addition to another order, I will reply to you, Chiang Kai-shek Zheng Can Yin.

Provisional Municipal Conference of the Municipal Government 124

The Municipal Government held a provisional municipal conference on December 19th, 1930. The attendees were Yu Hongjun, Xu Pei Huang, Sun Baorong, Zhu Yan, Tang Naikang, Pan Gongzhan, Shen Yi, Yuan Liang, Hu Hongji, Huang Boqi, and Xi Dingmo. The observers were Qian Yongming and Xu Fu. The chairman was the Mayor and the secretary was (Yuan Shenglu). (A) Matters for Report. (1) Report of the Chairman. The construction of the central area of this city is the only large-scale project to implement the Great Shanghai Plan. Since the 123rd Municipal Conference on July 5th of last year and the 124th Municipal Conference on July 12th of the same month passed the decision, the Municipal Central District Construction Committee was established to actively plan and proceed within the time limit. Over the past year, the facilities that should have been in place within the time limit have already achieved considerable results. However, since this matter involves the construction of people's lives, and the stone is awaiting the lifting, it is difficult to expect it to be implemented soon without a complete and concrete plan and a determination of the steps to be taken. Therefore, the Municipal Conference was convened to discuss the points that should be discussed in the implementation plan of the Municipal Central District Plan prepared by Director Shen of the Public Works Bureau, and the two Chairmen Yu of the Construction Discussion Committee of this Government and the Chairman Xu of the Municipal Bank were invited to participate in the discussion to ensure that there is a unified implementation plan and to determine the steps to be taken in order to proceed quickly. (2) Director Shen of the Public Works Bureau represented the opinions of the members of the Municipal Central District Construction Committee (the detailed text is printed separately). (B) Matters for Discussion. (1) Discuss the points that should be discussed in the implementation plan of the Municipal Central District Plan. It was resolved that the original proposals 1 and 2 should be discussed together. The Secretary-General Yu, Director Shen, Director Pan, Director Huang, and Director Tang were designated to contact various financial enterprises to negotiate and determine a plan, and to request the National Government for record. Regarding the third item of the original proposal, it was resolved to continue issuing municipal public bonds to carry out the construction of the central area, and to establish an organization committee by Chairman Xu, Chairman Yu, Vice Chairman Qian, Director Tang, and Director Zhu to plan and proceed. Chairman Xu was to convene the meeting. Regarding the fifth item of the proposal, it was resolved that the municipal government's houses should still be built according to the original plan, and the remaining bureaus should temporarily adopt temporary buildings. The construction cost should be limited to 500,000 yuan, and July 7th, 1931 was set as the date for the groundbreaking ceremony for the municipal government's houses. Regarding items 6, 8, and 9, they were deleted, and the remaining items 4, 7, and 10 were all passed in accordance with the original proposal. The articles are listed below. 4. The land for the construction of the municipal government should be acquired in advance so that it can be leveled for construction, and tree planting and etiquette can be held there in 1931. 7. Regarding the opening of a new commercial port, please hire experts to prepare a detailed plan in advance and designate a large part of the second phase of municipal public bonds to be used for the initial construction of the port. 10. In order to develop the central area of the city, incentives should be adopted, and the relevant bureaus should prepare separate plans for further discussion.

Chinese Concession Telephone Service to Remain Under Old Agreement for Now 128

Temporary Measures After Expiration of Old Agreement

The telephone agreement between the Shanghai Telephone Bureau of the Ministry of Communications and the Chinese and Foreign Telephone Company in the concession expired on December 17th of last year. However, this type of agreement was made between the former Ministry of Communications and the old company. Now that the old company has been sold, its validity has naturally been lost long ago. Therefore, the Shanghai Telephone Bureau has repeatedly submitted reports to the Ministry of Communications and specially consulted the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to negotiate with the old company. However, the so-called old shareholders and old company have been dispersed since the sale. Although the new company once submitted a request to the Ministry of Communications to sign a new agreement, the Ministry of Communications firmly refused on the grounds that the establishment of the new company involved infringing upon our sovereignty and naturally could not be regarded as a counterparty. Therefore, it has been delayed until now without any positive measures. It is now heard that the Shanghai Telephone Bureau and the Municipal Public Utility Bureau have jointly discussed a temporary measure to negotiate with the telephone company in the concession, which is to temporarily operate the Chinese concession telephone service under the old agreement during this period. Once the conversion of the Chinese telephone system to automatic machines is completed, all telephones in the concession that are installed in the Chinese territory will be removed. This measure has now been submitted by the Shanghai Telephone Bureau to the Ministry of Communications for approval.

Pacific International Academic Society 130

To be Held in China This Year

Preparations for the Chinese Branch

The Pacific International Academic Society, originally named the Pacific International Relations Discussion Group, has already held two general meetings and will be held in China this year. The location of the fourth general meeting is generally in Peiping [Beijing]. The Chinese branch of the society is located in Shanghai and has already begun preparing for the meeting. Yu Ri was appointed as the Executive Director, Zhao Jinqing as the Deputy Executive Director, and Fang Jiaobo, Wang Yunwu, Zhu Jingnong, Liu Hongsheng, Yu Qingtang, Xu Xinliu, etc. as the Executive Committee members. Liu Dajun was appointed as the Research Director, and He Lian, Pan Guangdan, He Dequan, Zhou Shouyi, Tao Gong, Zhang Yunhai, etc. as the Research Committee members. Chen Liting was appointed as the Chief Secretary. The Pacific International Academic Society was first initiated by important leaders in the commercial and academic circles of Honolulu. The first general meeting was convened in Honolulu from July 1st to 15th, 1925. A total of 112 representatives from nine countries, including China, Japan, the United States, Korea, Canada, Australia, New Zealand, Hawaii, and the Philippines, attended the meeting. The Chinese branch also gathered public organizations in Shanghai in February of the same year and elected more than 30 committee members to organize the Chinese Preparatory Committee. After the opening of the first general meeting, the Chinese branch was established. The second general meeting was held again in Honolulu from July 25th to 29th, 1927. That year happened to be the beginning of the Chinese political upheaval, and the issues discussed at the meeting mostly focused on Chinese politics. The United Kingdom also joined the meeting that year. The third general meeting was convened in Nishikyo, Japan from October 28th to November 9th, 1930. There was a lot of research on Chinese issues, and the Chinese representatives invited the fourth general meeting to be convened in China this year. The society was initiated by the people of the countries along the Pacific Ocean. Its purpose is to discuss the crux of international issues among the countries along the Pacific coast in the capacity of individual citizens. The society's organization is a committee system. Its highest organ is the General Committee of the Pacific International Academic Society, which is composed of one representative jointly recommended by the participating countries. The branches in each country are organized by the committees elected by each country. In addition to holding a general meeting every two years, the society also focuses on research and publication, and specially hires famous domestic experts to actively engage in it. The projects that are currently underway are: "The Current Situation of Our Country's Industry" by Nankai University in Tianjin, "The Utilization of Our Country's Fields and Acres" by Jinling University in Nanjing, "The Investment Situation in Our Country" by Liu Dajun, Director of the Statistics Department of the Legislative Yuan of the National Government, "The International Relations of the Three Eastern Provinces" by Yenching University in Peiping and Nankai University in Tianjin jointly, "Our Country's Diplomatic Problems" by Bao Mingqian of Peiping University and Xia Jinlin of Guanghua University in Shanghai jointly. The above-mentioned research is always written into papers by those in charge for reference at the general meeting. In addition, famous experts are hired to write special books, hoping to study together with the society and the people.

Ten Priests and Nuns Describe Abduction Experience After Escaping Danger 131

Will Return to Xunyang After Resting in Shanghai for Two Weeks

The Shanghai Evening Post reports that four Catholic priests and five nuns who were abducted in Ji'an, Jiangxi on October 4th of last year arrived in Shanghai on Sunday (11th) afternoon on the Nanjing steamer after being rescued from the Donggu bandit's lair by government troops two days before Christmas. It is said that the treatment in the bandit's den was quite good. These bandits and communists are under the command of Peng Dehuai and Zhu De. In the first month, the priests and nuns were assigned to care for the wounded in the Red Army Hospital on Qingyuan Mountain (transliteration). The hospital was in a pagoda with limited facilities and many wounded. In early November, they were transferred to the Red Cross team and set off with the bandit army. In the next five weeks, they trekked through the mountains, which was extremely difficult, especially for the women. On December 12th, the bandits abandoned them in a mountain cave near Donggu, and no one guarded them anymore. The weather was very cold at that time, and they only had withered grass to keep warm, and there was not much food left. The situation was conceivable. Finally, on December 23rd, they caught a glimpse of a team of soldiers on the horizon crossing the ridge. At that time, they knew that government troops were chasing the bandits, but they did not know what kind of troops were coming. They ventured to the nearby hilltop and waved a Red Cross flag to summon them. Soon, four people came forward, and after learning that they were the 18th Division of the Provincial Army, they were rescued. They then took a gunboat to Zhangshu Town, and then took a car to Nanchang, and then took a boat from Jiujiang to Shanghai. They have now been resting in Shanghai for two weeks and will return to Jiujiang to inspect the situation in the interior of Jiangxi Province, and then go to preach again.

Real Estate Association Letters Fei Xindun 132

1. Water Supply Contract

2. Concurrent Salaries of Employees

3. Allowing Dog Racing Tracks

The Shanghai Real Estate Association sent a letter to the Director General of the Shanghai Public Concession Board yesterday, stating, "Dear Mr. Fei Xindun, Sir, since you assumed the position of Chairman of the Shanghai Public Concession Board and now Director General, all your measures, whether meritorious or sinful, will be judged by the public. There is no need to repeat them. However, our association is driven by the concept of public interest in three major events in your political achievements, and it is like a bone stuck in the throat. It seems that it is necessary to urge you to pay attention. Please forgive us for being frank. (1) The contract signed with the British Shanghai Water Company did not pay enough attention to the interests of taxpayers, namely (A) the guaranteed interest rate is too high, (B) the right to issue bonus shares, (C) the company's property, namely the water supply equipment, is given to the shareholders, (D) in addition to the guaranteed interest rate, the shareholders can be given bonuses again, (E) the capital is calculated in gold. Therefore, taxpayers have not been able to enjoy the benefits of public monopoly undertakings today, but have suffered the damage of increased burdens. (2) Destroying the good habits of the Public Concession Board by appointing paid employees as representative directors of the British Shanghai Water Company, and it is said that this matter was requested by the company, which is even more suspicious. (3) Allowing the establishment of dog racing gambling tracks, which has caused great harm to the public. The Public Concession Board is now facing major difficulties in banning them. If it had been given careful consideration that day, and the interests of the public had been carefully weighed, there would have been no such mistakes. Although you, as the representative of the Public Concession Board, are not legally responsible for the above three major events, (1) and (3) have harmed the citizens and trapped the Public Concession Board. The second event has created suspicion of bias on the part of the Public Concession Board towards the water company, and the long-standing good habits have been destroyed. The responsible parties should express their responsibility. Because we love you deeply, we cannot help but speak frankly, and we especially want to advise you against acting rashly and violating public anger, which are the ancient precepts that politicians should take as a great warning. We respectfully wish you a happy new year. The Shanghai Real Estate Association, January 13th, 1931."

Foil Industry Association Appeals for Fellow Traders 133

Please Municipal Chamber of Commerce to Telegraph Finance Ministry for Sympathy

The Foil Industry Association sent a letter to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, stating, "Urgent, To the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce, Sir, In order to relieve the suffering of merchants and the people, our government implemented the cessation of Likin [internal transit tax] from January 1st, 1931. Under orders, the sea was filled with joy. According to the original plan decided by the Five Provinces Likin Cessation Committee, tinfoil should be subject to a special consumption tax in the place of production. After one tax, it can be circulated freely throughout the country without being taxed again. However, according to a telegram report from Shaoxing, Zhejiang, the new regulations have not yet been announced, and tinfoil has stopped loading and shipping. The news came, and we were greatly shocked. This city's tinfoil shops handle a large amount of tinfoil, all of which depend on Shaoxing for supply. Transportation has been suspended for more than ten days. The existing stock is exhausted, and new goods have not arrived. Letters and telegrams have been sent to urge, but there is no solution. The market is tense, and people are panicked. Looking back at all industries, goods can continue to be loaded and shipped without being affected by the cessation of Likin. Only our foil industry is restricted, and the source is cut off. We are shocked and uncertain. If this continues, all the foil shops in the city will inevitably have no goods to sell and will close down one after another. We have always admired your association's leadership of the merchants and your responsibility to relieve the suffering of merchants and the people. We respectfully request that you report the situation to the Ministry of Finance and ask for sympathy for the merchants' difficulties, and lift the tinfoil ban, and allow the goods to circulate freely together with the goods of other industries, so as to stabilize business and reassure the people. We are waiting anxiously for orders. The Shanghai Municipal Foil Industry Association Preparatory Office bows, Yuan."

Social Bureau Bans Obscene Books

On December 9 of last year, the Municipal Social Bureau discovered that local newspapers were carrying advertisements for the book "Love Tide" published by the Xinzhi Bookstore. Fearing that it would be detrimental to public morals, it notified the newspapers to stop running the advertisements and instructed the bookstore to submit the book for inspection. Subsequently, the bookstore submitted the book to the bureau, which sent it to the relevant department for review. It has now been reported that the book is divided into three volumes, A, B, and C. Volumes A and C do not contain obscene content, but Volume B contains accounts of lewd activities, which are indeed detrimental to public morals and are in accordance with the provisions of Article 2, Paragraph 1 of the city's regulations on banning prohibited advertisements in newspapers. After review, there was no objection. The bureau ordered the bookstore to recall and destroy all copies of "Love Tide" B that had been sent out, and sent personnel to the bookstore to retrieve 13 copies of "Love Tide," which were destroyed in public. The bureau also sent letters to various newspapers to prevent the book from being sold through advertisements in local and out-of-town newspapers and harming young people.

University Student Ni Guangxun Still Missing

Ni's Wife Due to Give Birth Any Day

Ni Guangxun, a graduate of Chih Tze University, left his wife without saying goodbye in the autumn of last year. It has been four months since then. Details were previously reported in the newspaper. His wife, Fan, who was six months pregnant, gave birth to a son last month and now has two sons and two daughters. However, Ni's whereabouts are still unknown. Although his wife has asked people to search for him everywhere, there has been no news. Fan previously submitted a petition to the city's Women's Association, suspecting that Ni's sister was concealing information, requesting the association's assistance to avoid being unable to rely on living expenses in the future. The association sent letters to Ni's sister and brother-in-law, ordering them to come to the association for questioning. However, Ni's sister ignored them. Now that Fan has given birth, it is said that Ni's sister, due to the persuasion of many people, is willing to give Fan 1,000 yuan to sever the relationship with Ni. However, Fan is demanding 4,000 yuan, so the matter has not been resolved yet.

Xihufang Housing Association Opposes Rent Increase

The houses in Xihufang, Ximen Road, French Concession, belong to a Chinese man named Shen. They were built only three years ago. Now, because the landlord suddenly increased the rent, the tenants rose up in protest upon hearing the news. On the one hand, based on the order of the French Consul General to ban landlords from increasing rent, they sent a letter to the accountant of the building, Da Li, to persuade the landlord to automatically cancel the rent increase. On the other hand, they sent letters to the Chinese Taxpayers Association and other organizations, requesting assistance, which was very firm. It is said that they have organized an association to deal with this matter. All the tenants insisted that not only would they not recognize the rent increase, but also because the rent was already higher than that of neighboring areas, they would submit a petition for rent reduction.

Page 16

It has already been determined that Shen Jiazhen and Pan Zhenya, tenants of the neighborhood, will be representatives to handle the matter.

Guangfuli Rent Increase Lawsuit

New Sassoon Increases Rent Again and Again

The tenants petitioned for exemption. The Guangfuli real estate on Guangdong Road is owned by New Sassoon, a British company. It was renovated and completed in 1925. The rent was already high. The monthly rent for a three-story house was 122 taels, 80 taels for a two-story house, and 40 taels for a one-story house. Unexpectedly, in August 1928, the foreign firm again notified the tenants to increase the rent: an additional 15 taels per month for a three-story house, 10 taels for a two-story house, and 5 taels for a one-story house. Otherwise, they would have to move out. At that time, all the tenants wanted to settle the matter and endured the pain of paying the increase, but unanimously declared to the owner that the rent would not be increased again within five years. Only two years later, on August 1 of last year, New Sassoon broke its promise and increased the rent again by 20% of the original amount: an additional 9 taels per month for a one-story house, 18 taels for a two-story house, and 27 taels for a three-story house. The tenants believed that the owner was greedy and increased the rent again and again, wanting to drive the tenants to their deaths.

It was difficult to bear the burden. The tenants jointly organized a tenants' association and elected representatives to negotiate with New Sassoon, asking them to consider the difficult business situation and cancel the rent increase, and continue to collect rent at the original amount. The foreign firm refused the request and stopped collecting rent. The tenants expected that they would use the excuse of unpaid rent to file a lawsuit. They deposited the rent due in the Zhongnan Bank every month. As expected, they were sued for unpaid rent in the Special District Local Court. Yesterday, the tenants hired Liang Bohua as their lawyer to appear in court to state the reasons for requesting exemption from the rent increase, asking the court to order the plaintiff to continue to collect rent at the original amount and bear the litigation costs. The plaintiff's lawyer claimed that the rent increase was due to the high land price. Judge Xu instructed that the verdict would be announced at a later date.

Xue Family Property Dispute Settled

Xue Baorun, a wealthy paint merchant living in the Xiahui Road area of the French Concession, died of illness last year. Because Xue had an concubine outside and Xue Gu Qiaolin gave birth to a son named Baobao, he hired a lawyer last year to file a complaint in the French Concession Court against his legal mother, Sun, and brothers, Jiasheng, Gengsheng, and Yansheng, for seizing the property. At the end of last year, Judge Gong ordered a summons for questioning. However, because the defendant's lawyer's defense procedures were not yet complete, he requested an extension of one week for another summons. It is now known that this case has been mediated by friends of both parties, and a settlement was reached with more than 100,000 yuan as the settlement condition. Yesterday, the lawyers of both parties completed the notarization procedures, and the case is now concluded.

Framing Someone by Planting Stolen Goods Backfires

Sentenced to Six Months Imprisonment

Wang Honggui from Jiangbei has been unemployed for a long time and has been wandering in Shanghai, associating with bandits and developing bad habits. Recently, he has been intimidating and extorting honest people among his fellow villagers in the Yangshupu area. On the evening of the 20th of last month, because his neighbor Zhao Heizi refused to be extorted, Wang Honggui took a piece of worn clothing and placed it outside Zhao's door, trying to lure Zhao's 15-year-old son, Hongbao, to pick it up in order to carry out his cunning plan of framing Zhao Hongbao for stealing clothes. The Yangshupu Police Station sent detectives to investigate and found out the truth, releasing Zhao's son and arresting Wang. He was sent to the Special District Local Court, where Judge Feng interrogated him. Yesterday morning, he was sentenced to six months in prison. Harming others harms oneself. It can be said that he brought it upon himself.

Key Suspect in Four Banks Robbery Arrested in Suzhou

Hua Guibao from Wuxi, a bandit who, in March of last year, colluded with bandits who had been captured by the police and sent to the Special District Local Court to rob a huge amount of money from the Shanghai Four Banks Preparation Treasury, escaped to Suzhou and lived freely. Recently, the Public Security Bureau detectives arrested Hua. When the Hongkou Police learned of this, they prepared a document and sent Detective Liu Yongxiang to Suzhou to bring Hua back to Shanghai. The police chief ordered him to be detained for further investigation.

Unnamed Man Found Frozen to Death

Near the 17th telegraph pole near the Meijialong Station of the Shanghai-Hangzhou Railway, an unnamed man, about 40 years old, bald, barefoot, wearing a torn black cotton robe and blue cotton pants, was found frozen to death. After investigation, a railway worker reported to the stationmaster, who sent police to take care of the body and ordered the local bailiff, Mei Xiaomao, to report to the Local Court for an autopsy. At 11:00 a.m., the court sent prosecutor Li Gongchen and forensic doctor to conduct an autopsy, confirming that the man had frozen to death. No family members were found to claim the body. The local bailiff asked the Tongren Fuyuantang to provide a coffin for burial.

Notorious Bandit Xu Wenbin Escapes

Xu Ruqing, Who Leaked Information, Arrested

Xu Wenbin, a notorious bandit from Rugao, was hiding outside the West Gate of Shanghai on Luban Road. The Public Security Bureau learned of this and sent detectives and police officers from the Liyuan Road Police Station in the Second District to arrest him on the previous day. Unexpectedly, Xu Ruqing went to leak the information, causing Xu Wenbin to flee. Xu was intercepted by the detectives and sent to the Public Security Bureau for interrogation. Yesterday, he was transferred to the Local Court for interrogation.

Zhang Ajing Rescued After Jumping into the Huangpu River

Zhang Ajing from Songjiang worked as a coppersmith in an electric tram company. Because he had no family in Shanghai, he stayed at his sister Gu Zhang's house at No. 9 Hede Road, North City. However, Zhang and Ajing had incompatible personalities and often quarreled. A conflict broke out again over a trivial matter a few days ago. Ajing was so resentful that he suddenly had the idea of committing suicide. He took a car to the Santai Wharf in the South City and jumped into the Huangpu River. With a loud splash, he sank to the bottom of the river. Fortunately, Ma Longyun, a watchman at the 17th post, heard the sound and immediately rushed to rescue him. After being rescued ashore, he was frozen due to the severe cold and became unconscious. After receiving medical treatment and resuscitation, he was taken to the First Precinct of the First District. The police chief sent the police to Zhang Gu's house to notify her to come to the station to claim him.

Wife Leaves and Never Returns

Husband Files for Divorce

Xu Jianting, a 51-year-old tea server at the Xujiahui Catholic Church, recently hired Xu Zuoliang as his lawyer to sue his wife, Xu Gu, in the Local Court for taking their two daughters and fleeing without a trace, requesting a divorce. This morning, Judge Ding Ruku opened the court for trial. The defendant's address was unknown, so a summons was not issued. Xu Jianting's attorney, Ren Enji, appeared in court. Xu Jianting testified that he had been married to the defendant for more than 20 years and had two daughters and one son. He worked at the Catholic Church and was unable to go home often. The defendant had been unfaithful in recent years and had improper behavior. In February 1928, she took the two daughters and fled with all their clothes and jewelry. He had searched everywhere without success and had requested the court to issue a public notice, but there was still no news. The defendant had been away from her husband for more than one or two years, which showed that the relationship between husband and wife had been broken. Moreover, the defendant often borrowed money from his friends and relatives, and creditors often came to him to demand repayment. He was really burdened and had to request a divorce. The judge then invited prosecutor Wu to the court to state his opinion, saying that the defendant Xu Gu had been away from her husband for more than two years, and there was no longer any affection between husband and wife. He asked the presiding judge to rule according to law. The lawyers for both parties stood up to debate each other. The judge then declared the debate in this case closed and adjourned for judgment.

Wall Collapses and Injures Pedestrian

Yesterday afternoon at 1:20 p.m., the street-side wall of the stone-frame houses at Nos. 6 to 11 Tongde Lane, Bansongyuan Road, Nanshi, collapsed due to years of disrepair. Ren Wenhui was sent to the hospital for treatment. It was found that the owner of the house was Hu Baoli from Anhui, who lived in the Wantai Candy Store in Liguangqiao, Nanshi. The Wang District Chief of the Second District reported the case to the Inspectorate by telephone and ordered the landlord to be brought to the station for investigation.

Shanghai Bank Sues Liquidators

Arising from Failure to Distribute Funds Equally

After the Zuitian Restaurant went bankrupt, lawyers Wu Chengyu and accountant Huang Rixin were hired to jointly liquidate the assets. The creditors, upon hearing the news, all reported the debts owed by Zuitian to the liquidators. Wu and Huang acknowledged the debts and said that after Zuitian was sold and the proceeds were received, the funds would be distributed to the creditors proportionally. Later, Wu and others repeatedly invited the creditors to meetings. The Hongkou branch of the Shanghai Commercial and Savings Bank, as a creditor, was owed more than 5,739 yuan in overdrafts. The branch sent representatives to attend each meeting, and Wu and Huang did not object to this debt at first. However, after Zuitian's assets were sold and the proceeds were collected, only 30% of the small debts were paid in full. The branch inquired with the liquidators, who initially did not respond. Later, they claimed that the branch's debt was guaranteed by someone else and that the liquidators were not responsible for this debt. The branch did not agree and hired lawyer Qian Baohe to sue Wu Chengyu and Huang Rixin in the Special District Local Court, requesting that they be treated the same as other creditors and be repaid 30% of the debt, totaling 1,731 yuan, 7 jiao, and 3 li. If there were no remaining funds in the liquidation to pay, the defendants should be held liable for compensation in accordance with Article 184 of the Civil Code, and the two defendants should submit the liquidation accounts in full for verification. If there were any remaining funds, they should be distributed proportionally according to the amount of debt to protect the rights. Yesterday morning, Judge Xu Wenrong specially opened the Seventh Court for trial. The defendants did not appear, and each hired a lawyer to appear in court to defend them. First, the staff of the Hongkou branch of the Shanghai Bank presented account books to prove the amount of debt and the repeated attendance at meetings. Then, the lawyers of both parties debated one after another. Judge Xu adjourned the court for judgment on the 19th of this month.

A Glimpse of the Inland Waterway Ice Interruption

Six Ships in Huzhou Blocked by Ice

The weather has been unusually cold in recent days, and the inland river ports have all frozen over. Most of the small steamers from Shanghai to Jiangnan and Zhejiang have been suspended. There are six shipping companies operating between Shanghai and Huzhou, divided into early and late shifts. Since yesterday, due to the ice blockage of the waterway to Lili, the small boats traveling to and from have been unable to pass. As a result, the six companies operating between Shanghai and Huzhou have completely suspended their services yesterday. Passengers received refunds, and goods were returned to customs.

Suzhou Ships Unable to Pass

There are three local small steamers operating between Shanghai and Suzhou, divided into single and double shifts, with more cargo than passengers. Unexpectedly, the Shanghai-Suzhou route was also interrupted yesterday due to the freezing of the inland river. Those that departed the day before were stranded on the way. The Zheng steamers that were supposed to depart today have also announced their suspension because the ships from Shanghai have not arrived. Passengers and cargo that urgently need to be transported to Suzhou mostly switched to the Shanghai-Nanjing Railway yesterday.

Hangzhou Ships Unable to Arrive

Although the Shanghai-Hangzhou ships have not been blocked by ice, the ships that were supposed to arrive in Shanghai yesterday have not arrived even late at night. It is still unknown whether they will arrive in Shanghai today. If there are no ships arriving in Shanghai today, this route can only be suspended until the weather warms up and the ice melts.

Wuxi Ice Interruption for Five Days

Yesterday, local inland river shipping companies received a telegram from Wuxi stating that the inner ports of the four townships of Wuxi have been blocked by ice for five days. Most of the small boats in Wuxi have suspended their services. Please temporarily store the goods from Shanghai to the Wuxi countryside. They also received a telegram from Baoying stating that the canal has also been frozen for five days, and the local civil aviation boats have all been suspended.

Local News Two

Prevention and First Aid for Coal Gas Poisoning 138

Notice from the Municipal Health Bureau

The Shanghai Municipal Health Bureau issued a notice saying: Citizens, this Bureau has heard that tragic incidents of death from coal gas poisoning frequently occur in this city. In the past, similar tragedies often occurred in places like Beijing. Later, with experience, people learned prevention and first aid methods, and this harm has been greatly reduced. This Bureau now specially explains it to everyone: (1) Causes of poisoning: Coal balls or coal blocks emit a gas called carbon monoxide when they are not burned to a very bright state. This gas is colorless and odorless, making it often difficult to detect. If inhaled in large quantities, breathing will become rapid, the face will turn red, and one will feel dizzy and confused, as if drunk. Severe poisoning can lead to death, and even mild cases can cause illness for several days. (2) Prevention methods: When burning coal or charcoal in a room, be sure to install a chimney or exhaust pipe. If there is no chimney or exhaust pipe, it must be burned in a well-ventilated area outside the house until it is very bright before moving it indoors. The same should be done when adding coal. Also, when coal is burning indoors, one or two of the windows along the ceiling must be opened to allow air circulation and exchange between the indoor and outdoor air. It is best not to burn coal at night while sleeping. If it is still burning, the doors and windows must not be tightly closed to prevent ventilation. In short, when burning anything in a room, be sure to allow the outdoor air to circulate and exchange fully with the indoor air. People in the room should also go outdoors often to relax. (3) First aid for poisoning: If someone unfortunately suffers from coal gas poisoning, quickly move them to a well-ventilated area, loosen their clothes, and perform artificial respiration. The method is as follows: Loosen the poisoned person's clothes, lay them flat, and raise their back with pillows or other objects to allow their lungs to expand. Stand behind their head, slowly lift the poisoned person's arms forward, extend them overhead, and then slowly lower them to the sides of the ribs, gently pressing down. Repeat this process until the poisoned person wakes up. After waking up, it is still necessary to seek medical treatment to recover to health, otherwise, hidden diseases may develop, so be careful. It is best to provide first aid while quickly seeking a Western doctor for examination. The above is very basic knowledge, but because some people do not understand it, tragic news of death from coal gas poisoning often occurs. This notice is intended to remind everyone to pay attention at all times and not be careless. This is a special notice.

Explosion at Dada Tobacco Factory Causes Disaster 139

Many Workers Scalded

Due to Carelessness of the Watchman

At the Dada Tobacco Factory at 35B Tangshan Road yesterday afternoon, an explosion occurred in a steam boiler, injuring twelve male and female workers, who were all sent to the hospital for treatment. Among them, the female worker Wang Xia suffered burns to both eyes, and there is a risk of blindness. The other workers are not seriously injured. The cause of the accident and the injuries of the workers are recorded below.

Steam Boiler Explosion: The steam boiler that caused the explosion was used to heat and mix spices when making cigarettes. It was installed downstairs in a tin-covered room. Recently, the factory has been very busy manufacturing cigarettes for other companies. Because the contracting party sent their own workers to watch over the steam boiler, yesterday afternoon at around 3:00 PM, the watchman left the room to talk to someone. It turned out that a long time passed, and he did not return, causing the heat inside the steam boiler to become excessive and unable to escape. It exploded upwards. By the time other workers noticed and came forward to help, it was already too late. The steam cover rose, broke through the floor boards, and affected the workers in the tin-covered room.

Worker Injuries: After the floor boards were broken through, three workers were injured and fell to the ground. However, the male and female workers working in the spice room downstairs were also largely affected because they could not escape. Most of them suffered from being hit by hot water or objects on their heads, faces, ears, and eyes. The workers in the tobacco silk room were also largely affected. In total, twelve male and female workers were injured, three of whom were on the upper floor, and the rest were working downstairs. After the accident, the factory reported it to the police, who used vehicles to send the workers to Renji Hospital and Guangren Hospital for treatment. One of the female workers, Wang Xia, 27 years old, suffered the most severe injuries to both eyes. Other male and female workers, such as Lu Jiebin, Shen Ayou, Shen Yinmei, and Zhou Weng, suffered injuries to their waists, legs, faces, and other parts, but were not seriously injured. Four people were in Tongren Hospital, and the rest were in Guangren Hospital.

Smuggling Chinese to France 140

Discovered After Arriving in France

Chen Yaotang's Crime is Unpardonable

Chen Yaotang, a Qingtian native residing at 4 Qingxuefang, Yimiaonei, claims to be in the remittance business, specializing in remitting money for fellow villagers going abroad, but secretly colludes with crew members of French postal ships to smuggle passengers (smuggling passengers means bribing crew members to hide fellow villagers in the cabin to go abroad). A month ago, eleven fellow villagers bribed a crew member of a certain French ship to hide in the cabin to go to France. Because the wharves in Shanghai were heavily guarded and there was no opportunity to take advantage of, he first sent the fellow villagers to Hong Kong to board the ship. Unexpectedly, after arriving in France, the French detectives discovered that the eleven Chinese had no passports and immediately detained them in the police station. They confessed that Chen Yaotang had contacted the crew members to arrange for them to be hidden in the cabin to go to France for half the fare. The French police went to arrest the crew members, but they had already fled. The French police then requested the Minister to France, Gao Lu, to send a telegram to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, which was forwarded to the Shanghai Municipal Government, ordering the Municipal Public Security Bureau to quickly arrest and severely punish Chen Yaotang, who was smuggling passengers, to prevent ignorant and foolish people from being deceived and ending up stranded in a foreign country. It is reported that the Municipal Public Security Bureau, after receiving the order, has arrested Chen Yaotang and is dealing with him severely.

Four More Cases in the Past Two Days

In the past two days, four more ship accidents occurred in the Huangpu River. They are recorded below:

Tugboat Collides with and Damages Coal Ship: At around 3:00 PM the day before yesterday, a coal ship hired by Kai Ping & Co., loaded with 50 tons of coal, was sailing north in the Yongjiang South section. When it reached Longmao Wharf in Lujiazui, Pudong, it was suddenly hit by the Taikoo Company's Zhuting tugboat, damaging two masts, the front and rear beams, and the deck, causing a loss of over 70 yuan.

Huge Wave Sinks Paper Boat: Xi Jinsheng, a runner for the Xiexiang Public Customs Brokerage Firm, ordered boatman Xi Kunquan to load 32 pieces of paper at around 5:00 PM the day before yesterday and sail to the vicinity of Osaka Wharf in Pudong. At that time, a tugboat from Dala Company sped past, causing a huge wave that sank the paper boat. It soon floated to the surface, but the paper was ruined.

Large Ship Sinks Small Ship: The Nissin Company's Daikichi Maru ship arrived in Shanghai at 6:00 PM the night before last and reached Osaka Wharf in Pudong. When anchoring and turning around, it accidentally hit the Chengtong small ship moored at the wharf, causing the entire ship to take on water and sink to the bottom. Yesterday, the ship's captain, Zhou Chaosheng, reported the incident to the Water Police Station for record, so that he could claim compensation from the company of the ship that caused the accident.

Tugboat Damages Two Ships: The Jardine Matheson Tugboat Company's tugboat towed the Dehe ship south from the Xiang Sheng Iron Factory in Lujiazui, Pudong at 11:00 AM yesterday. When it reached the corner of Lujiazui, it accidentally hit the bow of Ding Guichun's brick boat moored there, damaging it. The stern of the brick boat was pushed inward, and it hit the stern of a Chongming fishing boat, damaging it. The victims reported the incident to the Water Police Station for investigation.

Extension for Closure of Two Greyhound Racing Tracks 144

Reply to the Municipal Council Still Pending

Representatives of the Shanghai Times newspaper visited Mr. McBain, the Chairman of the Ming Garden Greyhound Racing Track, and Mr. Evans, the secretary of the Shen Garden Greyhound Racing Association. Both stated that they had not yet drafted a reply to the Municipal Council's letter ordering them to stop holding greyhound racing events within the Public Concession by March 31st of this year.

Ratepayers' Association Requests Immediate Closure of Greyhound Racing Tracks 145

The Ratepayers' Association sent a letter to the Public Concession Municipal Council yesterday, stating: "Regarding the ban on gambling within the Concession, this Association has sent repeated letters to your Board since 1928, requesting strict prohibition. In our letter of October 25th last year, we stated that the prohibition of gambling should begin with the closure of the greyhound racing tracks. We now see in the Western newspapers of the 10th of this month that your Board's ban on the large-scale greyhound gambling tracks will be delayed until March 31st of this year. Furthermore, the sites of these greyhound gambling tracks must contribute funds to relocate the tracks, and the employees of each track must be considered if they have difficulties. This is incomprehensible. It is evident that your Board is actively working to prohibit gambling and illegal entertainment venues that cause all kinds of evils, but a satisfactory solution has not been reached. However, it is not easy. However, your Board's current difficulties in closing the large-scale greyhound gambling tracks are self-inflicted. If your Board had not allowed the Greyhound Racing Association to establish large-scale greyhound gambling tracks in the first place, this kind of difficulty would never have occurred. Considering the current deterioration of Shanghai society and the implications in the declaration of a certain police chief in New York City, those responsible for allowing the establishment of large-scale greyhound gambling tracks should bear at least some moral responsibility. Furthermore, if the gambling tracks are deemed harmful to the public interest, they should be closed immediately. Otherwise, allowing the gradual theft of one chicken per day will become allowing the theft of one chicken per month. Contributing funds to relocate the sites and providing solutions to the difficulties of the track's employees is akin to rewarding organizations that engage in activities that harm the public interest, which is not something that municipal authorities should do. In the world, is there any municipal authority that knowingly allows those who harm the public interest to extend the period of harm? We hereby send this letter, hoping that you will take it into consideration. In terms of law and reason, the large gambling tracks should be closed immediately so that they no longer harm the public interest."

Municipal Public Works Bureau Urges Removal of Coal and Charcoal from Wharf 146

Enforcement Will Be Carried Out After Deadline

There are Chai and charcoal shops such as Gonghe Xing, Hong Ji, and Qia Ji on the pier bank of Wharf Nos. 5, 6, and 7 of the South Shanghai Wharf in this city. Initially, they all subleased the gaps in the head from Dada Company to store firewood and charcoal. Due to overloading, the pier bank is gradually collapsing and the situation is very dangerous. In addition, the firewood and charcoal shops stack goods as high as the roof, which affects the appearance of the wharf and fire prevention. After the former port authority took over Dada Wharf, it ordered them to move. As the merchants expressed their difficulties, a special extension was granted until the end of 1930. Now that the wharf management matters have been transferred to the Municipal Public Works Bureau, the merchants have reapplied for renewal of the lease. The Bureau has rejected the application and has set a deadline for all of them to move out. If they fail to do so, the Public Security Bureau will be notified to enforce the removal in order to ensure the safety of the embankment.
